class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Boston_Globe&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston Globe">Boston Globe</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t<div dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American daily newspaper</div>\n<table href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_the_United_States" title="List of newspapers in the United States">List of newspapers</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><i><b>The Boston Globe</b></i> is an American daily <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspaper</a> founded and based in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>. The newspaper has won a total of <a href="#Pulitzer">26 Pulitzer Prizes</a>, and had a weekday circulation of 92,820 during the final three months of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-watson_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watson-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Boston Globe</i> is the oldest and largest daily newspaper in Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Founded in 1872, the paper was mainly controlled by <a href="/wiki/Irish_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Catholic">Irish Catholic</a> interests before being sold to <a href="/wiki/Charles_H._Taylor_(publisher)" title="Charles H. Taylor (publisher)">Charles H. Taylor</a> and his family. After being privately held until 1973, it was sold to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> in 1993 for $1.1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion, making it one of the most expensive print purchases in U.S. history.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The newspaper was purchased in 2013 by <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool F.C</a>. owner <a href="/wiki/John_W._Henry" title="John W. Henry">John W. Henry</a> for $70<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million from <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Company" title="The New York Times Company">The New York Times Company</a>, having lost over 90% of its value in 20 years.\n</p><p>The newspaper has been noted as "one of the nation\'s most prestigious papers."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 1967, <i>The Boston Globe</i> became the first major paper in the U.S. to come out against the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-new_yorker_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_yorker-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The paper\'s 2002 coverage of the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse_scandal_in_the_Catholic_archdiocese_of_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual abuse scandal in the Catholic archdiocese of Boston">Roman Catholic Church sex abuse scandal</a> received international media attention and served as the basis for the 2015 American drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Spotlight_(film)" title="Spotlight (film)">Spotlight</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The chief print rival of <i>The Boston Globe</i> is the <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Herald" title="Boston Herald">Boston Herald</a></i>, which has a smaller circulation that is declining more rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Editor-in-chief" title="Editor-in-chief">editor</a> of <i>The Boston Globe</i> is <a href="/wiki/Brian_McGrory" title="Brian McGrory">Brian McGrory</a>, who took the helm in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" pages</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#August_2018_campaign"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">August 2018 class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Websites"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Websites</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a class="toctext">Stat</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png/200px-1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="437" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png/300px-1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png/400px-1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png 2x" data-file-width="508" data-file-height="1110" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1896_BostonDailyGlobe_ad_Bradley_His_Book_v1_no2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An advertisement for <i>The Boston Globe</i> from 1896, boasting of the largest circulation of any newspaper in New England</div></div></div>\n<p><i>The Boston Globe</i> was founded in 1872 by six Boston businessmen who jointly invested $150,000 (equivalent to $3,201,250&#32;in 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-Hatic_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hatic-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The founders included <a href="/wiki/Eben_Dyer_Jordan" title="Eben Dyer Jordan">Eben Dyer Jordan</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Marsh" title="Jordan Marsh">Jordan Marsh</a> department store, and <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_Wakefield" title="Cyrus Wakefield">Cyrus Wakefield</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Rattan_Company" title="Wakefield Rattan Company">Wakefield Rattan Company</a> and namesake of the town of <a href="/wiki/Wakefield,_Massachusetts" title="Wakefield, Massachusetts">Wakefield, Massachusetts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>3\xe2\x80\x935</span></sup> The first issue was published on March 4, 1872, and sold for four cents (equivalent to $0.85&#32;in 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-Hatic_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hatic-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In August 1873, Jordan hired <a href="/wiki/Charles_H._Taylor_(publisher)" title="Charles H. Taylor (publisher)">Charles H. Taylor</a> as temporary business manager; in December, Taylor signed a contract to be general manager of the paper for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-Hatic_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hatic-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> He would serve as the first <a href="/wiki/Publisher" class="mw-redirect" title="Publisher">publisher</a> of <i>The Boston Globe</i> until his death in 1921, and was succeeded by four of his descendants until 1999.\n</p><p>Originally a morning daily, the <i>Globe</i> began a Sunday edition in 1877. A weekly edition called <i><b>The Boston Weekly Globe</b></i>, catering to mail subscribers outside the city, was published from 1873 until being absorbed by the Sunday edition in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>101</span></sup> In 1878, <i>The Boston Globe</i> started an afternoon edition called <i><b>The Boston Evening Globe</b></i>, which ceased publication in 1979. By the 1890s, <i>The Boston Globe</i> had become a stronghold, with an editorial staff dominated by <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish American Catholics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Boston_Globe_Building.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Old_Boston_Globe_Building.png/180px-Old_Boston_Globe_Building.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Old_Boston_Globe_Building.png 1.5x" data-file-width="256" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Boston_Globe_Building.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old <i>Globe</i> headquarters in downtown Boston on <a href="/wiki/Washington_Street_(Boston)" title="Washington Street (Boston)">Washington Street</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1912, the <i>Globe</i> was one of a cooperative of four newspapers, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Daily_News" title="Chicago Daily News">Chicago Daily News</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Globe" title="The New York Globe">The New York Globe</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Bulletin" title="Philadelphia Bulletin">Philadelphia Bulletin</a></i>, to form the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Newspapers_(U.S.)" title="Associated Newspapers (U.S.)">Associated Newspapers</a> syndicate.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1940_Massachusetts_gubernatorial_election" title="1940 Massachusetts gubernatorial election">1940 Massachusetts gubernatorial election</a>, the <i>Globe</i> correctly projected the re-election of Republican incumbent <a href="/wiki/Leverett_Saltonstall" title="Leverett Saltonstall">Leverett Saltonstall</a>, using methods first established by Charles H. Taylor; rival <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Post" title="The Boston Post">The Boston Post</a></i> called the race incorrectly for Democrat <a href="/wiki/Paul_A._Dever" title="Paul A. Dever">Paul A. Dever</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1955, <a href="/wiki/Laurence_L._Winship" title="Laurence L. Winship">Laurence L. Winship</a> was named editor, ending a 75-year period of the role being held by the paper\'s publishers.<sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>447</span></sup> In the next decade, the <i>Globe</i> rose from third to first in the competitive field of what was then eight Boston newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-retire1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retire1-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1958, the <i>Globe</i> moved from its original location on <a href="/wiki/Washington_Street_(Boston)" title="Washington Street (Boston)">Washington Street</a> in downtown Boston to <a href="/wiki/Morrissey_Boulevard" title="Morrissey Boulevard">Morrissey Boulevard</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Boston" title="Dorchester, Boston">Dorchester</a> neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1965, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Winship" title="Thomas Winship">Thomas Winship</a> succeeded his father as editor. The younger Winship transformed the <i>Globe</i> from a mediocre local paper into a regional paper of national distinction. He served as editor until 1984, during which time the paper won a dozen <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prizes</a>, the first in the paper\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Boston Globe</i> was a private company until 1973 when it went public under the name <b>Affiliated Publications</b>. It continued to be managed by the descendants of Charles H. Taylor. In 1993, <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times_Company" title="The New York Times Company">The New York Times Company</a> purchased Affiliated Publications for <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1.1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion, making <i>The Boston Globe</i> a wholly owned subsidiary of <i>The New York Times</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> parent.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The Jordan and Taylor families received substantial The New York Times Company stock, but by 1999 the last Taylor family members had left management.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Boston.com" title="Boston.com">Boston.com</a>, the online edition of <i>The Boston Globe</i>, was launched on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Consistently ranked among the top ten newspaper websites in America,<sup id="cite_ref-:2_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> it has won numerous national awards and took two regional <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Awards</a> in 2009 for its video work.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Boston Globe</i> has consistently been ranked in the forefront of American journalism. <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine listed it as one of the ten best US daily newspapers in 1974 and 1984, and the <i>Globe</i> tied for sixth in a national survey of top editors who chose "America\'s Best Newspapers" in the <i><a href="/wiki/Columbia_Journalism_Review" title="Columbia Journalism Review">Columbia Journalism Review</a></i> in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Under the helm of editor <a href="/wiki/Martin_Baron" title="Martin Baron">Martin Baron</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Brian_McGrory" title="Brian McGrory">Brian McGrory</a>, the <i>Globe</i> shifted away from coverage of international news in favor of Boston-area news.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <i>Globe</i> reporters <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rezendes" title="Michael Rezendes">Michael Rezendes</a>, Matt Carroll, <a href="/wiki/Sacha_Pfeiffer" title="Sacha Pfeiffer">Sacha Pfeiffer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walter_V._Robinson" title="Walter V. Robinson">Walter Robinson</a> and editor <a href="/wiki/Ben_Bradlee_Jr." title="Ben Bradlee Jr.">Ben Bradlee Jr.</a> were an instrumental part of uncovering the <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse_scandal_in_the_Catholic_archdiocese_of_Boston" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexual abuse scandal in the Catholic archdiocese of Boston">Roman Catholic Church sex abuse scandal</a> in 2001\xe2\x80\x932003, especially in relation to Massachusetts churches. They were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> for their work, one of several the paper has received for its investigative journalism,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and their work was dramatized in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Academy Award-winning</a> film <a href="/wiki/Spotlight_(film)" title="Spotlight (film)"><i>Spotlight</i></a>, named after the paper\'s in-depth investigative division.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>The Boston Globe</i> is credited<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2016)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> with allowing <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gammons" title="Peter Gammons">Peter Gammons</a> to start his <i>Notes</i> section on baseball, which has become a mainstay in many major newspapers nationwide. In 2004, Gammons was selected as the 56th recipient of the <a href="/wiki/J._G._Taylor_Spink_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="J. G. Taylor Spink Award">J. G. Taylor Spink Award</a> for outstanding baseball writing, given by the <a href="/wiki/BBWAA" class="mw-redirect" title="BBWAA">BBWAA</a>, and was honored at the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> on July 31, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Savage" title="Charlie Savage">Charlie Savage</a>, whose reports on <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">President Bush</a>\'s use of <a href="/wiki/Signing_statement" title="Signing statement">signing statements</a> made national news, won the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_National_Reporting" title="Pulitzer Prize for National Reporting">Pulitzer Prize for National Reporting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg/250px-Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg/375px-Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg/500px-Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boston_Globe_building_Sept_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The newspaper\'s <a href="/wiki/Morrissey_Boulevard" title="Morrissey Boulevard">Morrissey Boulevard</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Boston" title="Dorchester, Boston">Dorchester</a> in September 2009. In 2017, the newspaper moved its printing operations to <a href="/wiki/Taunton,_Massachusetts" title="Taunton, Massachusetts">Taunton</a> and its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Boston" title="Downtown Boston">Downtown Boston</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>As of 2010, the <i>Globe</i> hosted 28 <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blogs</a> covering a variety of topics including <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Boston" title="Sports in Boston">Boston sports</a>, local politics, and a blog made up of posts from the paper\'s opinion writers.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 2, 2009, The New York Times Company threatened to close the paper if its unions did not agree to $20 million of cost savings.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Some of the cost savings include reducing union employees\' pay by 5%, ending pension contributions, ending certain employees\' tenures.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Boston Globe</i> eliminated the equivalent of 50 full-time jobs; among buy-outs and layoffs, it swept out most of the part-time employees in the editorial sections. However, early on the morning of May 5, 2009, The New York Times Company announced it had reached a tentative deal with the Boston Newspaper Guild, which represents most of the <i>Globe</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> editorial staff, that allowed it to get the concessions it demanded. The paper\'s other three major unions had agreed to concessions on May 3, 2009, after The New York Times Company threatened to give the government 60-days notice that it intended to close the paper.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Despite the cuts helping to "significantly [improve]" its financial performance by October of that year, the <i>Globe</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> parent company indicated that it was considering strategic alternatives for the paper, but did not plan to sell it.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2011, <i>The Boston Globe</i> launched a dedicated, subscription-based website at bostonglobe.com.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Starting in 2012, the <i>Globe</i> provided a printing and circulating service for the <i><a href="/wiki/Boston_Herald" title="Boston Herald">Boston Herald</a></i>, and by 2013 was handling its rival\'s entire press run.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> This arrangement remained in place until 2018, ending after the acquisition of the <i>Herald</i> by <a href="/wiki/Digital_First_Media" title="Digital First Media">Digital First Media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_W_Henry-Fenway_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/John_W_Henry-Fenway_%28cropped%29.jpg/140px-John_W_Henry-Fenway_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/John_W_Henry-Fenway_%28cropped%29.jpg/210px-John_W_Henry-Fenway_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/John_W_Henry-Fenway_%28cropped%29.jpg/280px-John_W_Henry-Fenway_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1595" data-file-height="2124" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_W_Henry-Fenway_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_W._Henry" title="John W. Henry">John W. Henry</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In February 2013, The New York Times Company announced that it would sell its <b>New England Media Group</b>, which encompasses the <i>Globe</i>; bids were received by six parties, of them included John Gormally (then-owner of <a href="/wiki/WGGB-TV" title="WGGB-TV">WGGB-TV</a> in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Massachusetts" title="Springfield, Massachusetts">Springfield, Massachusetts</a>), another group included members of former <i>Globe</i> publishers, the Taylor family, and <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> principal owner <a href="/wiki/John_W._Henry" title="John W. Henry">John W. Henry</a>, who bid for the paper through the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Sports_Network" title="New England Sports Network">New England Sports Network</a> (majority owned by <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Sports_Group" title="Fenway Sports Group">Fenway Sports Group</a> alongside the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Bruins" title="Boston Bruins">Boston Bruins</a>). However, after the NESN group dropped out of the running to buy the paper, Henry made his own separate bid to purchase the <i>Globe</i> in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-globe-bids_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globe-bids-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-masslive-fenwaybid_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-masslive-fenwaybid-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> On October 24, 2013, he took ownership of the <i>Globe</i>, at a $70<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million purchase price,<sup id="cite_ref-sold_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sold-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-finish_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finish-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> and renamed the venture <b>Boston Globe Media</b>. On January 30, 2014, Henry named himself publisher and named Mike Sheehan, a prominent former Boston ad executive, to be CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-henryceo_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-henryceo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> As of January 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Doug Franklin replaced Mike Sheehan as CEO,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> then Franklin resigned after six months in the position, in July 2017, as a result of strategic conflicts with owner Henry.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, the 815,000-square-foot headquarters located in Dorchester was sold to an unknown buyer for an undisclosed price.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Globe</i> moved its printing operations in June 2017 to Myles Standish Industrial Park in <a href="/wiki/Taunton,_Massachusetts" title="Taunton, Massachusetts">Taunton, Massachusetts</a>. Also in June 2017, the <i>Globe</i> moved its headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Exchange_Place_(Boston)" title="Exchange Place (Boston)">Exchange Place</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Boston" title="Financial District, Boston">Financial District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Editorial_pages">Editorial pages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Editorial pages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_(final_paragraph).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_%28final_paragraph%29.jpg/220px-The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_%28final_paragraph%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_%28final_paragraph%29.jpg/330px-The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_%28final_paragraph%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_%28final_paragraph%29.jpg/440px-The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_%28final_paragraph%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="546" data-file-height="371" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Rise_and_Fall_Off_of_T._Reed_(final_paragraph).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Final paragraph of a March 1891 <i>Globe</i> editorial discussing <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Brackett_Reed" title="Thomas Brackett Reed">Thomas Brackett Reed</a>, signed "Uncle Dudley"</div></div></div>\n<p>Starting with the Sunday edition in 1891,<sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>75</span></sup> and expanded to weekday editions in 1913,<sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>176</span></sup> each lead editorial in the <i>Globe</i> was signed "Uncle Dudley", a practice ended by editor Thomas Winship in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 1980, the <i>Globe</i> published an editorial about a speech by President <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a>, which included the accidental headline "<a href="/wiki/Mush_from_the_Wimp" title="Mush from the Wimp">Mush from the Wimp</a>" during part of the press run, drawing national attention.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 1981, the editorial pages of the <i>Globe</i> have been separate from the news operation,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> as is frequently customary in the <a href="/wiki/News_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="News industry">news industry</a>. Editorials represent the official view of <i>The Boston Globe</i> as a community institution. The publisher reserves the right to veto an editorial and usually determines political endorsements for high office.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Globe</i> made its first political endorsement in 1967, supporting <a href="/wiki/Kevin_White_(politician)" title="Kevin White (politician)">Kevin White</a> in that year\'s <a href="/wiki/1967_Boston_mayoral_election" title="1967 Boston mayoral election">Boston mayoral election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Globe</i> has consistently endorsed Democratic presidential candidates,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> most recently <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_States_presidential_election" title="2016 United States presidential election">2016 presidential election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election" title="2020 United States presidential election">2020 presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Describing the political position of <i>The Boston Globe</i> in 2001, former editorial page editor Ren\xc3\xa9e Loth told the <a href="/wiki/Boston_University" title="Boston University">Boston University</a> alumni magazine:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>\nThe <i>Globe</i> has a long tradition of being a <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> institution, and especially on social issues. We are pro-choice; we\'re against the death penalty; we\'re for gay rights. But if people read us carefully, they will find that on a whole series of other issues, we are not knee-jerk. We\'re for <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">charter schools</a>; we\'re for any number of business-backed tax breaks. We are a lot more nuanced and subtle than that <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">liberal</a> stereotype does justice to.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Ellen Clegg, a long-time <i>Globe</i> journalist and former top spokeswoman for the newspaper, was named editor of the editorial page in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Clegg retired in 2019, and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Bina_Venkataraman" title="Bina Venkataraman">Bina Venkataraman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="August_2018_campaign">August 2018 campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: August 2018 campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In August 2018, the editorial board launched a coordinated campaign for newspapers nationwide to respond to President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>\'s "enemy of the people" attacks and "<a href="/wiki/Fake_news" title="Fake news">fake news</a>" rants against the media by publishing locally produced editorial responses on Thursday, August 16.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Within a couple of days, an estimated 100+ newspapers had pledged to join the campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> jumping to roughly 200 a few days later.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 13, the <a href="/wiki/Radio_Television_Digital_News_Association" title="Radio Television Digital News Association">Radio Television Digital News Association</a> and its Voice of the First Amendment Task Force encouraged its 1,200 member organizations to join the campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> while other media organizations also helped spread the call to action.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Even as some right-leaning outlets portrayed the <i>Globe</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s campaign as an attack on the president, rather than his rhetorical attacks on the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Estate" title="Fourth Estate">Fourth Estate</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> some newspapers got a head start, releasing content on August 15,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> while 350 newspapers participated in the event on August 16.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From August 10 to 22, approximately 14 threatening phone calls were made to <i>Boston Globe</i> offices.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The caller stated that the <i>Globe</i> was the "enemy of the people" and threatened to kill newspaper employees.<sup id="cite_ref-Ellement_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellement-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On August 30, California resident Robert Chain was arrested by an <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> <a href="/wiki/SWAT" title="SWAT">SWAT</a> team and charged with a single count of making a threatening communication in interstate commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-Ellement_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellement-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In May 2019, Chain pleaded guilty in a US federal court to seven counts of making threatening communications in interstate commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Magazine">Magazine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Magazine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Appearing in the Sunday paper almost every week is <i>The Boston Globe Magazine</i>. As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Veronica Chao is the editor, and contributors include <a href="/wiki/Neil_Swidey" title="Neil Swidey">Neil Swidey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meredith_Goldstein" title="Meredith Goldstein">Meredith Goldstein</a>.\n</p><p>Since 2004, the December issue features a <i>Bostonian of the Year</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Past winners include Red Sox general manager <a href="/wiki/Theo_Epstein" title="Theo Epstein">Theo Epstein</a> (2004), retired judge and Big Dig whistleblower <a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_Ginsburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Edward Ginsburg (page does not exist)">Edward Ginsburg</a> (2005), governor <a href="/wiki/Deval_Patrick" title="Deval Patrick">Deval Patrick</a> (2006), Neighborhood Assistance Corporation of America founder and CEO <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bruce_Marks_(Boston)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bruce Marks (Boston) (page does not exist)">Bruce Marks</a> (2007), NBA champion <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pierce" title="Paul Pierce">Paul Pierce</a> (2008), professor <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a> (2009), Republican politician <a href="/wiki/Scott_Brown_(politician)" title="Scott Brown (politician)">Scott Brown</a> (2010), U.S. attorney <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Ortiz" title="Carmen Ortiz">Carmen Ortiz</a> and ArtsEmerson executive director <a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_Orchard_(Boston)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Robert Orchard (Boston) (page does not exist)">Robert Orchard</a><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> (2011), Olympic gold medalists <a href="/wiki/Aly_Raisman" title="Aly Raisman">Aly Raisman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kayla_Harrison" title="Kayla Harrison">Kayla Harrison</a> (2012),<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> three people who were near the Boston Marathon bombing, Dan Marshall, Natalie Stavas, and Larry Hittinger (2013),<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/DeMoulas_Market_Basket" class="mw-redirect" title="DeMoulas Market Basket">Market Basket</a> employees (2014),<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Neuropathology" title="Neuropathology">neuropathologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Ann_McKee" title="Ann McKee">Ann McKee</a> (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-Swidey_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swidey-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> <span class="anchor" id="Pulitzer"></span>\n</p><p>On October 23, 2006, <i>The Boston Globe</i> announced the publication of <i>Design New England: The Magazine of Splendid Homes and Gardens</i>. This glossy oversized magazine is published six times per year.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pulitzer_Prizes">Pulitzer Prizes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Pulitzer Prizes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col">\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/1966_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1966 Pulitzer Prize">1966</a>:</b> Meritorious Public Service for its "campaign to prevent the confirmation of <a href="/wiki/Francis_X._Morrissey" title="Francis X. Morrissey">Francis X. Morrissey</a> as a Federal District judge."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1972_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1972 Pulitzer Prize">1972</a>:</b> Local Reporting, <i>The Boston Globe</i> Spotlight Team for "their exposure of political favoritism and conflict of interest by office holders in <a href="/wiki/Somerville,_Massachusetts" title="Somerville, Massachusetts">Somerville, Massachusetts</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1974_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1974 Pulitzer Prize">1974</a>:</b> Editorial Cartooning, Paul Szep.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1975_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1975 Pulitzer Prize">1975</a>:</b> Meritorious Public Service, <i>The Boston Globe</i>, for its "massive and balanced coverage of the Boston school desegregation crisis."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1977_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1977 Pulitzer Prize">1977</a>:</b> Editorial Cartooning, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Szep" title="Paul Szep">Paul Szep</a><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1980_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1980 Pulitzer Prize">1980</a>:</b> Distinguished Commentary, <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Goodman" title="Ellen Goodman">Ellen Goodman</a>, columnist.<sup id="cite_ref-Cops_His_Second_Pulitzer_page_6_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cops_His_Second_Pulitzer_page_6-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>1980:</b> Distinguished Criticism, <a href="/wiki/William_A._Henry_III" title="William A. Henry III">William A. Henry III</a>, for television criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>1980:</b> Special Local Reporting, <i>The Boston Globe</i> Spotlight Team for describing transit mismanagement.<sup id="cite_ref-Cops_His_Second_Pulitzer_page_6_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cops_His_Second_Pulitzer_page_6-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1983_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1983 Pulitzer Prize">1983</a>:</b> National Reporting, <i>The Boston Globe Magazine</i> for its article "War and Peace in the Nuclear Age".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1984_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1984 Pulitzer Prize">1984</a>:</b> Spot News Photography, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Grossfeld" title="Stan Grossfeld">Stan Grossfeld</a> for photographing the effects of the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pulitzer_Prize_page_21_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pulitzer_Prize_page_21-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>1984:</b> For Local Investigative Specialized Reporting, Kenneth Cooper, Joan Fitz Gerald, Jonathan Kaufman, Norman Lockman, Gary Mc Millan, Kirk Scharfenberg and David Wessel of <i>The Boston Globe</i> for a series on <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> including self-criticism.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.pulitzer.org/prize-winners-by-year/1984">[1]</a><sup id="cite_ref-Pulitzer_Prize_page_21_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pulitzer_Prize_page_21-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1985_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1985 Pulitzer Prize">1985</a>:</b> Feature Photography, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Grossfeld" title="Stan Grossfeld">Stan Grossfeld</a> for a "series of photographs of the <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9385_famine_in_Ethiopia" class="mw-redirect" title="1983\xe2\x80\x9385 famine in Ethiopia">1983\xe2\x80\x9385 famine in Ethiopia</a> and for his pictures of <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">illegal aliens</a> on the Mexican border." The Pulitzer was also awarded in equal parts to <a href="/wiki/Larry_C._Price" title="Larry C. Price">Larry C. Price</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Inquirer" class="mw-redirect" title="Philadelphia Inquirer">Philadelphia Inquirer</a></i> for his series on the war-torn peoples of <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1995_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1995 Pulitzer Prize">1995</a>:</b> Distinguished Beat Reporting, David M Shribman for his "analytical reporting on <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States" title="Politics of the United States">Washington developments</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States" title="Politics of the United States">national scene</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1996_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1996 Pulitzer Prize">1996</a>:</b> Distinguished Criticism, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Campbell_(journalist)" title="Robert Campbell (journalist)">Robert Campbell</a></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/1997_Pulitzer_Prize" title="1997 Pulitzer Prize">1997</a>:</b> Distinguished Commentary, <a href="/wiki/Eileen_McNamara" title="Eileen McNamara">Eileen McNamara</a></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2001_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2001 Pulitzer Prize">2001</a>:</b> Distinguished Criticism, <a href="/wiki/Gail_Caldwell" title="Gail Caldwell">Gail Caldwell</a></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2003_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2003 Pulitzer Prize">2003</a>:</b> Public Service, <i>Boston Globe</i> Spotlight Team for "courageous, comprehensive coverage in its disclosures of sexual abuse by priests in the Roman Catholic Church"<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2005_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2005 Pulitzer Prize">2005</a>:</b> Explanatory Reporting, <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Cook" title="Gareth Cook">Gareth Cook</a> for "explaining, with clarity and humanity, the complex scientific and ethical dimensions of stem cell research."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2007_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2007 Pulitzer Prize">2007</a>:</b> National Reporting, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Savage" title="Charlie Savage">Charlie Savage</a></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2008_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2008 Pulitzer Prize">2008</a>:</b> Distinguished Criticism, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Feeney" title="Mark Feeney">Mark Feeney</a></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2011_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2011 Pulitzer Prize">2011</a>:</b> Distinguished Criticism, <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Smee" title="Sebastian Smee">Sebastian Smee</a><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2012_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2012 Pulitzer Prize">2012</a>:</b> Distinguished Criticism, <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Morris" title="Wesley Morris">Wesley Morris</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2014_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2014 Pulitzer Prize">2014</a>:</b> Breaking News, for coverage of the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombing" title="Boston Marathon bombing">Boston Marathon bombing</a><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2015_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2015 Pulitzer Prize">2015</a>:</b> Editorial Writing, <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Kingsbury" title="Kathleen Kingsbury">Kathleen Kingsbury</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/2016_Pulitzer_Prize" title="2016 Pulitzer Prize">2016</a>:</b> Distinguished Commentary, <a href="/wiki/Farah_Stockman" title="Farah Stockman">Farah Stockman</a><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2016:</b> Feature Photography, Jessica Rinaldi<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_personnel">Notable personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Notable personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:The_Boston_Globe_people" Bacon">Edwin M. Bacon</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg/110px-Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg" decoding="async" width="110" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg/165px-Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg/220px-Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3596" data-file-height="5394" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pulitzer2018-marty-baron-20180530-wp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Martin_Baron" title="Martin Baron">Martin Baron</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <i>Globe</i> uses "editor" as the highest title (other newspapers may call this role <a href="/wiki/Editor-in-chief" title="Editor-in-chief">editor-in-chief</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The role of editor was held by three people in the earliest years of the paper, then from 1880 to 1955 by the publishers.<sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>447</span></sup> The extended period of a publisher-editor ended in 1955, when Laurence L. Winship was named editor by publisher William Davis Taylor.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>447</span></sup> Winship became the paper\'s top editor following the death of James Morgan, longtime <i>de facto</i> executive editor.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Morgan had joined the <i>Globe</i> in January 1884, hired by Charles H. Taylor.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>46</span></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Maturin_Murray_Ballou" title="Maturin Murray Ballou">Maturin Murray Ballou</a> (1872\xe2\x80\x931873)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edwin_M._Bacon" class="mw-redirect" title="Edwin M. Bacon">Edwin M. Bacon</a> (1873\xe2\x80\x931878)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edwin_C._Bailey" title="Edwin C. Bailey">Edwin C. Bailey</a> (1878\xe2\x80\x931880)</li>\n<li>Charles H. Taylor (1880\xe2\x80\x931921) <i>publisher</i></li>\n<li>William O. Taylor (1921\xe2\x80\x931955) <i>publisher</i></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Laurence_L._Winship" title="Laurence L. Winship">Laurence L. Winship</a> (1955\xe2\x80\x931965)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Winship" title="Thomas Winship">Thomas Winship</a> (1965\xe2\x80\x931984)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_C._Janeway" title="Michael C. Janeway">Michael C. Janeway</a> (1984\xe2\x80\x931986)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_S._Driscoll" title="John S. Driscoll">John S. Driscoll</a> (1986\xe2\x80\x931993)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Matthew_V._Storin" title="Matthew V. Storin">Matthew V. Storin</a> (1993\xe2\x80\x932001)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Martin_Baron" title="Martin Baron">Martin Baron</a> (2001\xe2\x80\x932012)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_McGrory" title="Brian McGrory">Brian McGrory</a> (2012\xe2\x80\x93present)</li></ul>\n<p>Source:<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyons_9-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyons-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>447</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_of_fabrication_and_plagiarism">Incidents of fabrication and plagiarism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Incidents of fabrication and plagiarism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1998, columnist <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Smith_(poet)" title="Patricia Smith (poet)">Patricia Smith</a> was forced to resign after it was discovered that she had fabricated people and quotations in several of her columns.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In August of that year, columnist <a href="/wiki/Mike_Barnicle" title="Mike Barnicle">Mike Barnicle</a> was discovered to have copied material for a column from a <a href="/wiki/George_Carlin" title="George Carlin">George Carlin</a> book, <i><a href="/wiki/Brain_Droppings" title="Brain Droppings">Brain Droppings</a></i>. He was suspended for this offense, and his past columns were reviewed. <i>The Boston Globe</i> editors found that Barnicle had fabricated a story about two cancer patients, and Barnicle was forced to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Columnist <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Jacoby_(columnist)" title="Jeff Jacoby (columnist)">Jeff Jacoby</a> was suspended by the <i>Globe</i> in 2000 for failing to credit non-original content used in his column.<sup id="cite_ref-CLTG_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CLTG-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In 2004, the <i>Globe</i> apologized for printing graphic photographs that the article represented as showing U.S. soldiers raping Iraqi women during the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> from a city councilor\'s presentation before they were verified. The photos had already been found by other news organizations to be from an internet pornography site.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the spring of 2005, the <i>Globe</i> retracted a story describing the events of a seal hunt near <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, that took place on April 12, 2005. Written by freelancer Barbara Stewart, a former <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> staffer, the article described the specific number of boats involved in the hunt and graphically described the killing of seals and the protests that accompanied it. In reality, weather had delayed the hunt, which had not yet begun the day the story had been filed, proving that the details were fabricated.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Columnist <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Cullen" title="Kevin Cullen">Kevin Cullen</a> was suspended by the <i>Globe</i> in 2018 for fabricating stories related to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Marathon_bombing" title="Boston Marathon bombing">Boston Marathon bombing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Websites">Websites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Websites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><i>The Boston Globe</i> maintains two distinct major websites: BostonGlobe.com is a subscriber-supported site with a <a href="/wiki/Paywall" title="Paywall">paywall</a> and content from the printed paper; and <a href="/wiki/Boston.com" title="Boston.com">Boston.com</a>, one of the first regional news portals,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> is supported by advertising. Between September 2011 and March 2014, the <i>Globe</i> gradually withdrew stories written by <i>Globe</i> journalists from Boston.com, making the sites more and more separated.<sup id="cite_ref-nieman-unbundle_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nieman-unbundle-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> BostonGlobe.com was designed to emphasize a premium experience focusing on content and emulating the visual appearance of <i>The Boston Globe</i> newspaper; the site was one of the first major websites to use a <a href="/wiki/Responsive_web_design" title="Responsive web design">responsive design</a> which automatically adapts its layout to a device\'s screen size. Boston.com followed suit in 2014. The two sites are aimed towards different readers; while Boston.com became targeted towards "casual" readers and local content, the new <i>Boston Globe</i> website is targeted towards the audience of the paper itself.<sup id="cite_ref-paidcontent-bostonglobesite_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paidcontent-bostonglobesite-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dotnet-responsive_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dotnet-responsive-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-poynter-globesite_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poynter-globesite-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Society_for_News_Design" title="Society for News Design">Society for News Design</a> selected BostonGlobe.com as the world\'s best-designed news website.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_subscriptions">Digital subscriptions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Digital subscriptions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In December 2016, the <i>Globe</i> reported a total of 72,889 "restricted digital access" subscriptions and this grew to 90,440 by the end of June in 2017. In a memo to the <i>Globe</i> staff on New Year\'s Eve of 2017, editor Brian McGrory said the newspaper was closing in on 95,000 digital subscribers and would pass the 100,000 mark in the first half of 2018. <i>Globe</i> spokeswoman Jane Bowman later confirmed that the <i>Globe</i> had reached the 100,000 goal. McGrory has stated in the recent past that reaching 200,000 digital subscribers would make the <i>Globe</i> self-sustaining.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Boston Globe Media Partners, which owns the <i>Globe</i>, operates a number of websites covering certain niche subjects. The sites share many resources, like office space, with the <i>Globe</i>, but are often branded separately from the newspaper:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Boston.com" title="Boston.com">Boston.com</a></b> is a regional website that offers news and information about the <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts" class="mw-redirect" title="Boston, Massachusetts">Boston, Massachusetts</a> area.</li>\n<li>Loveletters.boston.com is a love advice column run by <a href="/wiki/Meredith_Goldstein" title="Meredith Goldstein">Meredith Goldstein</a>, an advice columnist and entertainment reporter for <i>The Boston Globe.</i></li>\n<li>Realestate.boston.com is a regional website that offers advice on buying, selling, home improvement, and design with expert advice, insider neighborhood knowledge, the latest listings to buy or rent, and a window on the world of luxury living.</li>\n<li><b>BetaBoston,</b> launched in 2014, covers the local technology industry in Boston, its suburbs and <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crux">Crux</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Crux">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crux_(online_newspaper)" title="Crux (online newspaper)">Crux (online newspaper)</a></div>\n<p><i>Crux</i> was launched by the <i>Globe</i> in September 2014 to focus on news related to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nieman-unbundle_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nieman-unbundle-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-globecrux_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globecrux-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CruxAbout_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CruxAbout-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> At the end of March 2016, <i>The Globe</i> ended its association with <i>Crux</i>, transferring ownership of the website to the <i>Crux</i> staff.  With <a href="/wiki/John_L._Allen_Jr." title="John L. Allen Jr.">John L. Allen Jr.</a> as the new editor, <i>Crux</i> received sponsorship from the <a href="/wiki/Knights_of_Columbus" title="Knights of Columbus">Knights of Columbus</a> and several Catholic <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">dioceses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CruxAbout_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CruxAbout-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crux2016_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crux2016-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Crux2017_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crux2017-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stat">Stat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Stat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Stat_(website)" title="Stat (website)">Stat (website)</a></div>\n<p><i>Stat</i>, launched in 2015, covers health, medicine and life sciences, with a particular focus on the <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology_industry_in_Boston" title="Biotechnology industry in Boston">biotechnology industry based in and around Boston</a>. <i>Stat</i> employs journalists in Boston, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Boston_Globe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa Herald</a></i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Journal" title="The Boston Journal">The Boston Journal</a></i></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Post" title="The Boston Post">The Boston <i>Globe</i> held half-ownership of from 1966 to 1974</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
